Intermission VI

BGM: Drunk As I Like

"So Mister Rinnosuke, is this the game you wanted to show me?"

"Precisely. I remembered it when you bought that disc from me a while back. It was made by the same people. Thought maybe you'd like to try it..."

Behind the front counter at Kourindou, Sanae and Rinnosuke stood in front of a desk with a really old machine, a mottled off-white box with various buttons and holes hooked up to an old monitor, keyboard, and mouse on top. The shopkeeper holds the chair back for her, offering her a seat. Hesitantly, Sanae looks closely at the computer monitor and reads what seems to be the title of a game.

"M-Marathon? Eh?" she says, confused.

"Yep, that's correct. I prefer Quake, so I haven't really played much of it yet. Seems like a fine, but confusing game though." he explains to her.

"Yeah, I think you're right, Rinnosuke. I read in a magazine that this was one of the games they made before Halo. There's a lot of easter eggs and references to it in Halo, as well. It always sounded really mysterious, and you needed a really old kind of computer to play it, not an Xbox. I never thought you'd actually have it!" she explains.

Sitting down into the chair, the miko starts the video game up. After a short title card sequence, it sends her into the first level. Peering around the game world with the mouse, the screen displays a first-person view of an ugly, barren gray room made of metal from behind the ironsights of a gun... further squeezed inside decorative borders meant to look like some sort of futuristic device, with elements on the sides for health and weapons.

The game looked ugly. Really ugly, at least compared to Halo. Everything was dull gray, boxy, and pixelated. The view of the world was so small and blurry, compared to what Sanae was used to, that she couldn't even make out what she was looking at initially.

"I know it looks like this because it was made a long time ago, so I suppose I shouldn't judge it for that. Can I... play it, Mister Rinnosuke?"

He nods.

"I heard about what happened to your shrine. Sure, Halo 3 deserved to get destroyed for what it did to the noble first person shooter genre, but... even I can tell how happy you were with it. Go ahead and play for a while. It's the least I can do."

Sanae quickly gets engrossed in the mass slaughter of colorful pixelly aliens. They look like manga drawings coming to life and trying to kill her, and their bodies are turned to gorey paste against the floor with a satisfying audible splat. The same goes for the innocent humans, which Sanae kind of likes "accidentally" blowing up with bombs whenever they stand in a doorway or crowd in groups.

The game was confusing at points, interspersed with cryptic messages on ingame computer screens. The world resembled no practical space Sanae could ever imagine existing, with unwieldy strange tunnels, eerie empty rooms housing absolutely nothing, nonsensical raised platforms, and door switches placed high up on walls that had to be hit by a grenade launcher of all things to activate.

It was hard to tell if this space station was like this due to damage from the alien invaders, or if it had initially been designed to house real humans at all. It was more like a strange dream world than anything else. Were all old video games like this? The strangeness combined with brutal alien and random guy slaughter was plenty enough to keep Sanae interested for hours.

After going at it full throttle for a while, Sanae advances to the 13th mission, titled "Starship For Sale, Cheap". All the mission names in the game were weird like that. She runs the protagonist through zigzagging metal hallways, blasting aliens every step of the way. Eventually, she steps through a door into a small room, with two switches besides a large window into a bigger chamber.

Out of curiousity she presses one of the buttons. Inside the large room a huge metal pillar slowly rises out of the floor into the air. She presses it again, and the pillar freezes in place. Was this some sort of... puzzle? It didn't make sense to her, so she decides to save it for later.

Heading out of the room, she walks down another long corridor filled with aliens in need of killing. Fighting her way through, she runs through a u-shaped one with a button on the wall at the bend. Shooting it opens the door at the far end. Simple enough. She heads through, takes a right, and enters another observation room with more switches. It looks out into the same large chamber as before. She could even see the first room back on the far side. This time, she ignores it and heads back out.

Heading through more corridors, battling more aliens, Sanae takes another turn at a fork and comes into a third room, identical to the last two. What was the point of them? She didn't understand at all. She immediately heads back out and proceeds further through the level.

One last stretch of hall brings her right down into the chamber itself. Besides the one she already raised, there were five more still in the floor, and one raised in the center. On the opposite end, the level exit was etched into the sheer metal wall, too high up to enter from the floor.

Sanae realizes what she has to do. The pillars needed to be raised to form into a staircase she could walk up to reach the exit. To do this, she'd have to go back to all the rooms and raise each pillar successively higher than the last using the buttons. She needed to backtrack all the way to the start of the level where the first room was, then come all the way back. Irritating, but manageable since the enemies were dead already.

With a sign, she heads back and retraces her steps back through the level. When she reaches each room, she activates the pillars with the buttons, then stops them in place to form the staircase. In between, she has to wait for each each slow-moving lift and shoot buttons to open doors again. Upon reaching the first room and adjusting the pillars, she turns back again and heads through the level yet anoher time, waiting for the same lifts and shooting the same buttons she already had twice before by now. 

Finally, she returns to the large chamber. She tries to step onto the first pillar, only to bump into it to no avail! It was way too high for her character to step up. She had to go all the way back to the first room just to fix the first pillar!

"Aw, crap!" she sighs.

So she backtracks through the level again, dealing with the slow lifts and buttons, all the way back to the first room. There, she presses the button which makes the pillar sink back into the ground and start to rise again, then stops it lower than it was before. It was hard to judge precisely since the room was dark and the pillars far away, and she had to step away from the window to press the button, but she thought it was right this time. With a frustrated groan, she turns back and heads back through the level again, dealing with the lifts and the buttons once more.

Finally arriving in the big chamber again, she attempts to ascend her revised staircase. She steps up the first and second pillars, but falls down trying to ascend the third. The second step was too short to reach the next one, so she'd have to go back and fix it again. Groaning with frustration, Sanae slaps her forehead and heads back.

"Are you kidding me? This is soooo annoying!"

So she heads all the way back, adjusts the pillar, and returns again. Except she did it wrong, and it was now too high. So she heads back again, adjusts it, and returns yet again. She makes it to the middle pillar, only to discover the next three are too high as well. So she goes back and back again. Too low. Back and back again. Too high. Back and back again. Too high, still. Back and back again. The stairs were too low to reach the exit, so she had to fix the last three. Again. Back and back again...

Nearly half an hour and many, many grenades later, Sanae finally steps up the staircase of pillars into the exit room. Her muscles going slack with relief, she heaves a sigh and wipes sweat from her brow.

"Phew, glad that's over!" she remarks.

She doesn't notice the swarm of energy balls shooting towards her screen until half of them have already hit her character. The aliens hiding in the room ambush her while she's not paying attention, and make short work of the defenseless trooper. With a sudden yelp the game protagonist dies, Sanae watching in horror from his perspective as his body falls to the floor.

The game restarts from the last checkpoint. A save station in a hall at the start of the level. Meaning the pillars were completely reset to how they were in the beginning. She'd have to form the staircase all over again, painstakingly making sure each one was in the correct place. To do this, she'd have to traverse the metal hallways again, waiting for slow lifts and shooting buttons with the grenade launcher to open doors. Back and forth, again and again and again...

The miko stands up from the chair in a fit of rage! She angrily slams her fist against the desk, before turning away from the screen and towards the rest of the store, where the owner was busy cleaning a shelf.

"Dammit! Mister Rinnosukeeeee!!! Your game fucking suuuucks! I wanna play Halo 3 again!!!"

Something felt off to Cortana about the two Master Chiefs. They had been talking about youkai and fairies all day, for some reason. She searched through her memory banks for any mentions of this "Mr. Hat" person. No results. Just what was going on in their heads? This was starting to get irritating to the AI. If they didn't stop this soon, she might even turn evil for a plot twist and completely ruin the franchise with bad storytelling...

BGM: Blow Me Away (from "Halo 2")

"Oh this is such an awesome part! Listen, the best song is going to play!"

"The best song? Ooh, this is very exciting!"

The two gamers fight their way into a ceremonial mausoleum within the capital city of the alien empire. All around the large, circular room, the strongest alien enemies in the game are fighting... not them, but amongst eachother! Due to a civil war between the aliens, the enemy forces were split into two warring sides that would fight eachother before the player. For once, they could sit back and watch the enemies duke it out without worrying about snipers, or tanks, or any other hazardous nuisances!

"Whoaaaa, seeing them all fight eachother is so cool!"

"See, I told you that this part was awesome!"

As the guitar of the musical theme swells, the fighting in the center of the room kicks off. A group of ape-like creatures shoot bombs at another group of reptilian ones in shiny white armor, who fire back with plasma and lasers. The two of them stand near the entrance and watch the fight from safety. They looked at the television more like it was playing a movie than a video game.

One of the reptilian aliens strafes out of an alcove and blasts at the apes with a golden plasma cannon held over his shoulder. With a couple volleys, they are all blown up by green blasts of volatile energy, their ragdolled bodies sent flying high into the air and skidding against the floor. With the other aliens dead, the victors suddenly turn their attention to the players.

"Wort wort wort!"

"Ok, Koishi! Now!" Sanae exclaims!

The two of them split up and come at the group of enemies from two angles. Switching back and forth between guns, Koishi takes two of them out with the infamous noob combo technique. Taking advantage of the distraction, Sanae sneaks up close to them. She takes out the enemy with the cannon from behind with a stab to the back from a glowing blue energy sword. The final remaining enemy turns around to face her in a rage, dropping his plasma rifle and pulling out an energy sword of his own. While he roars a battle cry, Sanae sticks him with a plasma grenade, and hops backward as he explodes! With their triumphant victory, they are awarded with the rest of the song without interruption.

Sanae gives Koishi a high-five, and the two girls share a happy cheer!

"Great job, Koishi! That's the last of them. Once we head through the exit, the level ends!"

"Oh boy! I can't wait to see what the next mission is!"

"Well, it kind of sucks actually!"

"But Miss Sanae, you said that about all the missions so far!"

The Forerunner Keyship hurtles out of a massive slipspace rupture in close vicinity to the besieged human homeworld, Earth. UNSC and Covenant ships remain at war high above the planet's surface, exchanging deadly payloads of energy weapons and missiles.

"We've got a new contact, unknown classification!"

Fleet Admiral Lord Terrence Hood stands aboard the battle-damaged Cairo Station, within the control center. Scurrying crewmen and sparks fly around him in equal measure. He turns toward the crewman who gave the alert and issues him a new order.

"It isn't one of ours. Take it out."

On board the Keyship, Chief kneels down on the ground, holding in his hand a cool frog he found. The animal was suprisingly docile as he let it rest calmly in his hand. Patching his suit's transmitter in with the UNSC radio network, he rises to his feet and begins to speak.

"This is Spartan 117. Can anyone hear me? Over."

Upon hearing the Chief's voice, Lord Hood looks up from his gruff pacing. He turns over to the nearest crewman.

"Isolate that signal!"

Back on Delta Halo, Master Chief sits on the end of a pier on a lake, fishing. As he calmly holds his fishing rod in his hands, his black hat shades his eyes from the sun overhead. He listens as the Admiral speaks to him over the transmitter in his suit.

"Master Chief, you mind telling me what you're doing at that lake?"

The soldier turns to the green-haired girl with the third eye sitting next to him on the pier, excitedly kicking her legs back and forth over the edge. She looks back at him and pulls back the line of her fishing rod, showing him the fish she had caught with a proud grin. It was a large fish with dark blue scales that resembled a trout from Earth. He gives her a thumbs up, then returns his attention to Lord Hood.

"Sir, fishing."
